Crab Proverbs 195

— Mei Xue

As someone living a school life, I certainly don't have the leisure to hold crabs and appreciate chrysanthemums, but our professor of Chinese studies often gives us essay topics related to crabs. The old man has written the character "crab" on the blackboard two or three times. Alas! Pitiful! Pitiful! My mouth doesn't eat crab, but my eyes see the character "crab" on the blackboard, wouldn't I be drooling three feet? The article of four or five hundred words is not yet finished, but it is dripping wet on half of the page! What is this? This is the drool left over when writing the essay.

Although the crab did not reach my mouth, what the Wu proverbs said about this character "crab" did provide me with a lot of humorous material. Crab proverbs, such as "eat old crab," "crab hand," "beggars eat dead crabs, all are good," "lotus leaf wraps crab, the more it wraps, the more it isn't," these are the warnings against whoring, gambling, and eating. A young man loses himself to a lascivious woman, called "eating old crab," is the harm of liking prostitution. The surgery for getting a winning hand is not good, every bet is bound to lose, called "crab hand," is the harm of gambling. Being greedy and insatiable, regardless of hygiene, called "beggars eat dead crabs, all are good," is the harm of liking to eat. Specially seeking outward beauty, inevitably exposing the content, called "lotus leaf wraps crab, the more it wraps, the more it isn't," is the harm of liking to dress up.

Others, laboring in vain, called "cow eats crab," being at a loss, called "footless crab belly," going from bad to worse, called "one crab is worse than another," running errands for others, called "shrimp soldiers and crab generals," all the Wu proverbs that mention this character "crab" mostly have negative connotations and no praise. Only one sentence, "摸摸 a big crab out of a small hole," can encourage us young students. Now burying ourselves in hard work, the knowledge we gain may be small, but as long as we concentrate and persevere, we will eventually achieve great things. For example, we are studying engineering, and in the future, we will make a great contribution to engineering. Isn't this "摸摸 a big crab out of a small hole?" Thinking of this, I dare not let my appetite hinder my studies, and the saliva flowing on the paper gradually dries up.

御香縹緲錄 196

— Original work by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter Seventeen: The Palace Courtyards of Shengjing

Although we had arrived in Fengtian that day, after several days of long journeys, people were so tired that they were speechless. Everyone was hoping to rest as soon as possible. No matter how magnificent and moving the palace courtyards of Shengjing were, no one had the energy to carefully examine them. At most, we could only take a cursory glance, like riding a horse and looking at flowers, and consider that we had a considerable understanding of this new environment. Fortunately, we came today and do not plan to leave tomorrow. According to the Empress Dowager's estimate before departure, we plan to stay here for seven days. With seven days, it will be enough to wander around fully. But after tonight, everyone's energy will be fully restored, and tomorrow we can have a big stroll! I like strolling the most, I just can't wait to stroll today, but we who have official duties, how can we act freely? So I can only be patient and stroll again tomorrow.

But just wandering around these empty palace courtyards, can only know the surface of it. I can never be satisfied. I must find a way to know its history, and the history of everyone related to it, that is really interesting! However, very few people must know these histories. Among the many people who came with the Empress Dowager, maybe only one or two people can say a few words. And these one or two people—of course, Li Lianying and Qing Shan—are the roles that I am inconvenient or unwilling to approach too much. Even if I reluctantly ask them, they may not be able to give me a detailed answer. I think my father must be very clear, but he is not here at the moment. Then who else can I ask? Never mind, I am determined to try the Empress Dowager tomorrow. If I happen to catch her in a talkative mood, the result will definitely be very satisfactory! (170)

Seventeen Years Old 197

— Wo Fo

Sixteen years old is truly the most important turning point in life, because you embark on the road of light; or fall into the abyss of darkness, or even run into the grave, almost all of these steps are taken at sixteen.

Before sixteen years old, from the time you are born to sixteen years old, this period is spent laughing and jumping in the loving arms of your parents. Of course, you are well-fed, well-clothed, and everything is only pleasant, without worry, without suffering any blows, because worry or blows are borne by your parents. However, age will not allow you to always rely on your parents' arms. At the same time, the whip of life is also gradually being prepared to demonstrate to you as you get older. So at most by the age of sixteen, except for the sons of wealthy families, you will finally have to leave the loving arms of your parents and take your first step in life, embarking on your path of life.

Because it is the first step, it is the first step in your life in the world, you must not ignore its importance. What's more, the world in front of you is in a fierce battle where light and darkness have not yet been decided. At the same time, there are many monsters and snake spirits, moving around and harassing. They are all ghosts of darkness, they all stretch out their long claws, open their big mouths, to grab people and eat people. However, they all wear a mask, a tempting and anesthetizing mask, so it is not easy for people to see through, and instead they willingly walk into their circle, to fatten their teeth. As a result, they are victorious, but you are finished. However, is it okay for a person to end like this? Ending your life like this, how can you be worthy of yourself, worthy of your parents, and even more unworthy of society and the country! Therefore, if you want to give full play to the meaning of your life, you must pay special attention to your first step into the world. You should correct your intentions, be meticulous in your thinking, sharpen your vision, invigorate your spirit, and strive to fight against darkness, find the path of light and start walking.

Really, sixteen years old cannot be ignored at all, because that is when you will take your first step into the world.

Social Sketches

Famous Cities All Have Many Beggars 198

— Zhang Zhenlu

Those beggars in tattered clothes, who have just escaped from hell, are squeezed on the grand avenues that are like paradise, decorated with flowers and brocade. They not only destroy the beauty of the city, but also infringe on the public's time, hygiene, and the will for tranquility, etc., especially diminishing the international prestige of our country in places where Chinese and foreigners live together. We cannot sympathize with their situation and condone and tolerate them, allowing them to be natural.

The beggars on Nanjing Road are all rushing passers-by for money. Their targets are limited to passers-by, and they have not been seen bothering shopkeepers. Their purpose is cash. The usual mentality is that a copper coin is an obligation, and their main job is "rushing one"—in their jargon, called "rushing pigs," obviously a rogue's insulting term, not only making you lose money, but also treating you like livestock!

One of the beggars, about thirty years old, often half-opens and half-closes his eyes, and always has a short cigarette in the corner of his mouth. His face is mixed with the color of smoke and vegetables. He wears a short coat. This person has the most chances to be met. His characteristic is that he often seems to be closing his eyes to rest, but he can quickly catch up with you. At first glance, he chatters non-stop in a local accent. His voice is deliberately vague, but you can sometimes hear a word or two. Other beggars, when they are frustrated in their desires and discouraged, gradually move away and make defamatory remarks. This beggar, however, regardless of whether you are willing to give him money, sometimes starts chasing you and utters ugly and vicious words that can be heard. And regardless of whether you are male, female, old, or young, he dares to treat you all the same and chase and scold you. If the passers-by are women, he deliberately makes the vague voice clearer, so that people can recognize that in his scolding, there are also mixed with harassment, such as: "Grandma! Miss! Save me, this extremely poor person! You all abandon me!..." He probably relies on his dirty appearance and fallen status, expecting that people don't think it's worth arguing with him, or he is familiar with the public's psychology of enduring humiliation and bearing burdens, so he is so unscrupulous and accustomed to it!

There is also a female beggar, about forty years old, with a local accent. I remember that she seemed to have a pockmarked face. Her characteristic is that she can work hard at begging. She can chase you for a long distance, sparing no effort in her waist, feet, and mouth, until she gets the money. After she gets your giving, she meets you again in no time. It is understood that she has realized your generous nature, and she will definitely come to chase you again, even more closely, unless you repeatedly declare that you don't want to give any more. However, sometimes when she is chasing you and has not gained anything, if she finds that there is no hope on you after all, or if she suddenly encounters a passerby or a group of passersby who are more likely to give, she is also determined to give up on you and turn around to pursue others with a very familiar and brisk movement. I have seen her switching back and forth to chase several batches of benefactors in an instant, and the tone of her begging is also changing closely, which is interesting! I have also seen her several times搶搶before a group of poor people and demanding the leftover rice and vegetables from the rice carrier. She is really a hard worker in the begging industry, and can be called a "standard female beggar."

An elderly beggar, with a beard and a long shirt, has the appearance of an old gentleman. His accent, which is not easy to distinguish, is noisy in people's ears, which is too uncomfortable!

The three of them are permanent beggars on Nanjing Road, rain or shine, "Meeting you again at dusk." Their common point is to use tight chasing and annoying words, which are hated by people, as a means of obtaining copper coins—of course, they sometimes chase foreigners and strengthen their desires. When they are chasing, they must adopt the same speed as you. Closely following in your footsteps. In the dense crowd, if you accidentally encounter a special situation in front and your pace is hindered, their bodies will bump into you, or step on the heel of your shoe, or even rush in front of you—so, for the sake of being sensible, for the sake of conforming to the meaning of the word "chasing," they slow down, or retreat back, and restore the original state of walking and following, and their dirty bodies do not have to rub against your clothes very closely, which is impossible to avoid in a crowded environment. They have no disabilities, they have very strong foot strength and a very long speaking spirit, and they are willing to do this begging business of looking up to people. I think they must have understood the proverb "suffering for the sake of saving face," and are willing to "do the lowest business and earn the highest copper coins"; performing begging duties on Nanjing Road, the income should be considerable.

Free Talk

The Philosophy of the Lazy 199

— Xiang Yu

Perhaps it is an external reason—the environment is like this, perhaps it is an internal reason—the disposition is like this, born with a skeptical temperament, plus a pair of lazy bones. From the time I was a child, some older people considered me an incomprehensible and hopeless waste, because the great truths they told me, I neither believed nor practiced, and finally I even ridiculed them. For example, once a private school teacher, Mr. Jia, was an opium smoker. Once he saw me, he was probably full of opium at the time, and suddenly said to me with great interest, "You are a young man. Young people should be ambitious. Why are you so lazy?" I unceremoniously said to him, "My laziness is just like your opium smoking. This is my hobby. Since you can smoke opium, can't I be lazy?" After speaking, I turned my head and left. Later, he never mentioned my laziness again when he saw me. Another time, a certain Mr. Yi, who was indulging in pornography, saw me, and he put on a solemn and respectable attitude and said to me, "You have become lazier and lazier lately. You should also love yourself!" I replied casually, "What don't I love myself? At least I still keep myself clean and don't go whoring to the point of rotting my nose." This touched a sore spot, and he became angry and scolded loudly, but he was still a little ashamed, so he had to withdraw himself. This method of dealing with people was effective, and I often used this method to deal with those who liked to lecture me. People also felt that I was a little difficult to deal with, even though I was lazy. When they saw me, they didn't dare to put on the attitude of a gentleman, and I saved myself a lot of trouble.

Now that I am older, the degree of laziness is naturally deeper. However, I have recently understood some worldly ways. When friends kindly ask, "Why are you so lazy?" I am quite embarrassed to directly reprimand them, so I have to excuse myself by saying, "I am a person who is congenitally deficient and malnourished, so I have a lazy disease." But some insensitive friends still have to pursue it and say, "Looking at your face so ruddy and your body so strong, you don't look like a patient." I have no words to answer, even if I reluctantly say, "This is my philosophy of life." This myself also knows is deceiving, because lazy people have no philosophy at all. If lazy people have philosophy, they will not become lazy people, but will become philosophers. However, philosophers all advise people to be diligent and warn people against laziness. Have you ever seen a few philosophers praising laziness?

Unless it is like Ji Shuye of the Jin Dynasty who was decadent, naturally those who believe in Lao-Zhuang thought will praise laziness. The reason is that he himself is an extremely lazy person. In his Letter of Severance with Shan Juyuan (Tao), he said: "I was orphaned at a young age, and my mother and brothers spoiled me. I did not study the classics, and my nature was lazy. My muscles and flesh are relaxed, and my head and face are often not washed for fifteen days a month. I don't like to be suffocated, so I can't take a bath. Whenever I want to urinate, I endure it and don't get up, only getting up when my bladder is slightly turning..." The last few words really reveal the true nature of a lazy person. Summer is okay, but in winter, sleeping in bed, urinating is really a troublesome thing for lazy people. Lazy people mostly have this experience, and they will not get up to urinate unless it is absolutely necessary. If lazy people are not lazy, and they want to find an ancient person to be a model, then Ji Shuye is an interesting figure in history.

The year before last, the British philosopher Russell also had an article called In Praise of Idleness, published in the September issue of the Review of Reviews (British). He advised the leaders of youth associations around the world to rise up and persuade the youth of the world to be lazy. He believes that modern industry has developed so much that people should no longer spend all their time on earning a living as they did before, and especially should not spend countless amounts of money on wars. They should have some extra time to enjoy the pleasures of life. He also advocates that leisure should be for everyone, and that most people should not work excessively, while a few people exclusively enjoy leisurely work. This kind of modern philosopher's preaching is naturally much better than Ji Shuye's purely passive laziness. If lazy people need to have philosophy, then we can naturally copy Russell's words in their entirety. However, Russell also said that the countries of the Far East (China is naturally included) are still in the pre-industrial era, and the amount of surplus obtained from human labor is not much, so people in these countries should not be lazy, but should work hard to achieve industrialization, and then they can be lazy. We can see that Russell's praise of laziness has its objective conditions. In countries like ours, and people like us, I also say loudly that we should not be lazy. Although I am lazy, I can accept his words, but when objective circumstances do not allow industrialization, and the people of the country do not pay attention to the issue of industrialization, what can we do even if we are not lazy? So before this era comes, I still have to be lazy, because in my opinion, laziness is also a virtue. I think Russell's opinion is right, laziness should be praised.

"Drinking Tea" 200

— TK

The Ulaqi Desert (Part 2) 201

— Shi Dai

At this moment, only Ba Gulik has a disappointed look, and no one would have expected him to abandon that beautiful hope.

"Why did Bayan Wang take away one-third of the livestock before letting us set off to Dariganga?" This question has been sprouting in Ba Gulik's mind since yesterday, and at this moment it is expanding. He wants to find the answer to this question from all aspects.

So Ba Gulik wiped the sweat from his face with his shiny sleeves, looked attentively at his daughter Anila, and then turned his face to look at those people in purplish-red riding camels, at the sweating livestock, at this group ignited by the fire of hope... Finally, he saw Bayan Wang's envoy, Nuoyin, wearing the purplish-red clothes that Bayan had given him, shining with greasy light, carrying a gun on his back, urging the long line from behind with great power.

"Evoking emotions from the scene," Ba Gulik thought. When he was a child, he followed his grandmother, father, mother, and many other people from Bihartu to Nukutai Plain by order of Bayin Wang. The situation was exactly the same as now. Before leaving, Bayin Wang sent envoys to take away one-third of the herders' livestock. When they arrived at Nukutai, people quickly slaughtered all the livestock, and each person had only one horse or one camel left, or a cow or a sheep. The weather in Nukutai was so cold, and the livestock did not eat that kind of grass. Many of them starved to death. People ate all the livestock and then starved to death. Ba Gulik's family all died, and he alone rode a camel and escaped to the southern part of Nukutai Plain... This time, I am afraid that the tragedy will be repeated again! He found the accurate answer, and immediately changed from disappointment to anger. Before his eyes were dripping bloodstains, skinny zombies... He couldn't help but shouted:

—We have been fooled!

Like a bomb exploded in the crowd, sharp eyes hundreds, thousands, tens of thousands... shot all over Ba Gulik's body.

—We have been deceived! Bayan Wang tricked us out of our livestock, telling us to go to Dariganga to die!

—Is Ba Gulik crazy?

The tents had just been set up, and it suddenly became cold, followed by a strong wind, sand flying all over the sky, hitting the Mongolian yurts, making a rustling sound: the sun had long set, and darkness covered the desert, covered the sky, covered the Mongolian yurts! Covered...

The wind blew harder and harder, and the sand kept flying onto the Mongolian yurts. Someone was shouting outside:

—Zhakasai's tent was crushed by the sand! Zhakasai is trapped inside!

A commotion, children crying, women cursing the wind! Young people were digging up the collapsed Mongolian yurts.

…………………………

I don't know when, the commotion calmed down. Ba Gulik's anger has not stopped burning in his chest. He walked around in the Mongolian yurt for a while, sat for a while, and his thoughts seemed to be knotted in his heart.

His daughter Anila had already seen through her father's thoughts. This kind of thought slowly retreats down and easily turns into troubles! She knew her father's temper very well, and she couldn't bear the pain to entangle her father, so she said with a smile:

—Dad, it's been a tiring day, go to sleep early. Didn't envoy Nuoyin say that we can reach Dariganga tomorrow?

—Nuoyin's words must be unreliable. Dariganga is not paradise, it is hell for us herders! There will be nothing there! How can there be a treasure land in the world where it doesn't snow in winter! We have been deceived!

Anila's words not only failed to extinguish the fire of Ba Gulik's anger, but added fuel to the fire.

—Go to sleep quickly, Dad! Why be sullen!

Lying down with his daughter, closing his eyes, his heart was pounding, and when his daughter fell asleep, he quietly crawled out of the Mongolian yurt.

People were resting, the wind was roaring, the tyranny of darkness, the flying sand, everything was wearing away the night on the desert.

The next morning, two corpses were found lying in a pool of blood in envoy Nuoyin's tent. It was none other than Ba Gulik and envoy Nuoyin. The knife in Ba Gulik's hand was still held tightly. (End)

Talking About Superstition 202

— Fo Lang

It is not entirely true to think that only stupid people are superstitious. Often heroes are superstitious and understand the true principles of superstition.

Heroes refer to those who "know the times." Knowing the times must be a smart person. The superstition of smart people is definitely not a stupid thing.

I remember when I was young, reading Han Yu's Memorial Against Welcoming the Buddha's Bones, I felt that he did not believe in gods and Buddhas at all, and I admired him in my heart! Because in Han Yu's time, even the emperor loved monks and respected puppets, and wanted to carry the "dead Buddha" to the gate of the country, which can be said to be superstitious to the extreme, but Han Yu dared to risk the taboo and say a lot of great principles to break superstition, and to hit the emperor's nails, it was a bit like the upright appearance of starting the decline of the eight dynasties. But when I read his Crocodile Sacrifice, it was not the same thing at all. Such a gentleman who broke superstition went to Chaozhou to be an official, but instead of taking practical measures to eliminate the harm of crocodiles, he burned incense and prayed, and took the article to sacrifice to the crocodiles, telling them "rascally ugly creatures" to get out quickly, which was still superstitious. But the book clearly states that the crocodiles got out the next day, which really confused me at the time. But later, when I got older, I suddenly realized that Han Yu's later sacrifice to crocodiles was much smarter and more advanced than his earlier memorial against welcoming the Buddha's bones. Han Yu was demoted to Chaozhou because he lost his high official position for memorializing against welcoming the Buddha's bones. He therefore learned the trick of superstition. He knew that superstition was a very smart thing and could not blame the emperor, so he applied this magic weapon. The meaning of his Crocodile Sacrifice was probably that he knew that the local customs were a bit barbaric and was afraid of suffering losses, so he came up with this method to make a show of strength. This time, Han Yu was not doing something stupid. He inquired about the rise and fall of the tide, and deliberately fabricated an article, saying that he really scared the crocodiles away. In essence, the intention of the article was not this at all.

In this way, the meaning of superstition is to be explained to the point of "bewildering" people without "believing" themselves, in order to exert the highest meaning of superstition. In recent years, the superstition in your country has become more and more prosperous with the restoration of the old. From scientific spiritualism to chanting spells to resist the enemy, it is naturally a kind of clever trickery of smart people who know the times. It is said that the inventor of scientific spiritualism has earned a fortune of thirty to forty thousand yuan by relying on "Ouija board." His small trick has been successful. Here, I also thought of a ghost shadow posted in front of a photo studio on North Sichuan Road a few days ago. It is said that this ghost shadow—a blurred ghost head—was photographed from a camera in broad daylight. Therefore, many people are crowding in front of this photo studio every day, and a line of small characters next to the ghost shadow is: available for scientists to study, two dimes per sheet.

The owner of the photo studio is smart, the inventor of Ouija board is smart, the people who advocate Buddha's power to resist the enemy are smart, and even Han Yu's crocodile sacrifice is smart—however, there are many smart people in the world. Can the clever tricks of smart people ultimately confuse people into believing? The fox's bald tail, I think, will be revealed all at once.

Wandering Soul (2) 203

— Lu Fen

Tears shimmered in the hollows of his eyes, as if he had truly walked hundreds of miles, carrying a weary belly, both hungry and thirsty. A bloated light surfaced on his face, like a smile that wasn't quite a smile, perhaps a contempt and pity offered to passersby. He greedily watched the faces of the travelers hurrying past him. A voice emerged from beneath his ash-covered beard:

"Fragrant amulet, eh? Won't turn white... South Sea Guanyin fragrant amulet..."

It really did sound like it was coming from beneath his beard; it didn't sound like speech at all.

He was unlike the usual wandering hustlers, violent and unreasonable. Not grabbing pedestrians with shameless hands; or pulling in a so-called "decoy," using manipulative words and setting up traps to confuse people, then reaching into their pockets to take their money. His method was closer to begging. He said he wasn't a medicine peddler, but had been entrusted to handle things for someone else, and because he was short of travel funds on the way, he had to sell cheaply. Everyone else, he said, wasn't buying medicine, but rescuing someone in distress. The fragrant amulet was to be considered a gift of repayment.

He stuck out his index finger, poking his crooked nose, his unfocused eyes landing on those indifferent faces, waiting for the fish to swim into the net themselves. In truth, at that moment, he no longer resembled a person, but rather a bereaved dog.

A shallow smile convulsed and spread from beneath his stubble. He coughed, changing his spiel and tone, raising his voice slightly.

"This treasure," he pinched something like an olive pit and held it to the tip of his nose, saying, "comes from Mount Putuo in the South Sea, the Putuo Temple, planted by the old Mother Guanyin herself..."

Perhaps someone here would ask –

"The South Sea? Is that the South Sea of the Great South Sea Guanyin?"

This interruption stopped him. He carefully looked to see if the person wanted to buy, then, as if cheered up, bobbed his hairy head and replied:

"That's right."

Sometimes, he even chuckled to himself for a while. The speaker hesitated, looking at other people's faces, not wanting to buy. Perhaps he would even turn around and walk away on his own. But he didn't get angry because of this. He also knew that the person who had left would not come back to patronize him, so he didn't give that person another glance, and instead explained to the honest folks around him: this treasure blossoms and bears fruit every twelve years, cures all diseases, big and small, if you don't encounter it in ten years, it won't be cured in ten years, three will take care of it well... He even more generously crushed one of the beads in his hand and brought it close to everyone's nose, saying with great certainty:

"Come on, it really does have a minty coolness when you rub it on yourself... Don't be fooled, neighbors... Come on, come on..."

Rubbing the top of his head under the brim of his hat with his other hand, he suddenly got angry and shouted:

"Only selling ten, ten! Those who don't think it's expensive, come!"

Talks

No Need to Blame Heaven and Earth 204

— Chen

Our Doctor of Literature, Mr. Hu Shi, once led young people to resist the old society during the May Fourth Movement, and also advocated for the women's liberation movement, his reputation spread far and wide for a time. Presumably, he has now achieved perfect merit and virtue, and after having "tried" everything, he is now presenting a very optimistic view. Some time ago, the doctor said that Chinese women's liberation has made a lot of progress in the past twenty years, breaking the old family and old ethics, marriage and love are already free, women have participated in various social undertakings, economic independence, political equality, small feet have become big feet, and have made Chinese women the most beautiful women in the world, this is the recognition of the current women's liberation by Dr. Hu Shi, who advocated the new culture.

Because of his optimism, the doctor expressed his unique views on the current student unemployment problem, which is lamenting "no way out". According to the interview with the reporter of the Sixth and Daily Society, the doctor said: "I teach at Peking University, and I have seen many university graduates. Except for a very small number with special circumstances, most of them can find a decent job after graduation... The small number who cannot find employment are because their studies are not applicable, and their paths are relatively narrow. For example, Gu Jiegang changed from studying philosophy to studying history, and Chen Gongbo also changed from studying philosophy to engaging in industry." He also said that in order to enjoy work and have no fear of unemployment, the first thing is to have the ability and knowledge to do things. Every graduate of Yanjing University can be hired in advance by others because they can give society a good impression. On the contrary, those who cannot find employment should seek the reasons why they cannot find employment, and do not need to blame heaven and earth, but only blame themselves. If you have the ability, why worry about not having food to eat.

Seek everything from yourself, be strict with yourself and lenient with others, this is our full-fledged national essence's philosophy of life. Mr. Shi Zhi, who is a pioneer of young people, earnestly admonishes the young students who are currently "worried about not having food to eat" to introspect themselves. He is really worthy of his true colors, and I admire him very much. However, many young students who have already "blamed themselves" and have not "blamed heaven and earth" cannot "have no fear of unemployment," which makes me have to doubt the doctor's teachings, and I cannot help but express myself.

Indeed, as the doctor said, there are many people who have changed from studying philosophy to studying history and engaging in industry. We also see many Bachelor of Engineering and Bachelor of Science students who have studied abroad and university students who have gone to the political arena to become bureaucrats and politicians. However, this does not mean that they have "no ability and knowledge to do things," but rather it precisely illustrates that China's entire economy cannot develop under various internal and external shackles, and cannot accommodate so many people who have diplomas and want to eat. At present, many students in this economic panic have extremely condescendingly sold themselves, but it is still difficult to find a place to eat. In this way, asking them to "not blame heaven and earth" and "blame themselves" is either covering up the fact of general student unemployment, or advising people to be content to starve. Secondly, although some school graduates can be hired in advance by others, they are either lucky ones, or it is because of connections, so that they "have no worry about food;" or it is because of hometown friendships, family connections, etc., that they get a "good impression from society." Isn't it often heard that a certain organization has become a hometown association, an alumni association, or a certain ancestral hall?

The times have determined the inevitable fate of student unemployment. What is the use of advising many unlucky students who have no connections or opportunities to "not blame heaven and earth" and "blame themselves"?

River Scene Sketches 205

— Da Ye

The long-haired poet wandering on the banks of the Huangpu River hummed to himself in solitude:

(In the past! I was under the poetic moon, I was on the picturesque river; the boatman rowed us, Quli snuggled on my shoulder. She said this is not a dream! Love has grown in my heart. Now? She is as ruthless as flowing water, whispering love to others; she is happy but I am hurt, I painfully pretend to be wounded.)

The cotton-like October wind! Fluttered by the river.

—Quli!

Scarlet lips seared on the young man's well-shaved chin.

What? You said, you always call me like this. You look like you want something. Say it! What do you want?

The young man's palms were sweating. His mouth opened, but his chin trembled.

—Yes, my Quli, I think...

Under her high and broad chest, Quli's jewel-like big eyes secretly watched the young man's face, a face reddened by the burning of love.

Quli saw what was on his mind, reached out and turned his cheeks towards her, aiming at her seductive eyes.

—What are you thinking about! Look, in front of our eyes, this moving river view, how should we enjoy it!

—Yes.

—You come.

Quli dragged the young man to the pier. She waved to the sampan rower. The sampan rowed over.

Jumping into the cabin, Quli ordered the boatman to row around on the river as he pleased.

As the boat tilted, Quli pretended to be scared and fell into the young man's arms.

—I'm scared, hold me tight!

Holding a mysterious woman, the young man thought foolishly, thinking that since he met her, he had spent a lot of money! Although she was very affectionate to him, why did she always smile and not agree to get engaged?

Thinking, thinking, his body suddenly felt cold, and his pores opened!

—What's wrong? You're shivering.

Quli squeezed him tightly, she saw that his face looked a little different tonight, so she reached out again to stroke his cheeks.

However, the young man continued to think about his doubts, he thought, did Quli really love him?

Page 19

—Quli, I know you love me, but...

The clever Quli seemed to not have noticed what he was saying, she was no longer afraid of the water and splashed the water on the edge of the boat.

—Look, the moon is so much fun in the water! Look, I'll grab it.

Saying that, she childishly let go of her hand and went to grab the water. The young man hurriedly grabbed her hand back.

—The water is cold, won't your hands get frostbite?

—No, with your passion, I don't feel cold at all.

The young man's face was unconsciously gloomy. Quli saw this and thought and thought, and suddenly told him that she had a good story to tell him.

But, Quli, who was busy all day long, what did she have in her mind? She thought for a long time before randomly pointing to the buildings on the land, saying how tall the houses were! Saying how red the neon lights were! Saying how many people were fishing with nets...

The young man's thoughts were shattered by her. He blankly followed her finger, watching the fishermen, watching the neon lights, watching the tall buildings, watching each pier, watching the long-haired man wandering alone on the pier, and it was as if he saw this long-haired man jump into the river, he was stunned.

Quli's laughter drilled into his ears again, she said:

—In this cool autumn night, there are still people coming here to swim, aren't they afraid of the cold? They're really cheap.

She also said that those who come here to swim are all lowly. Next summer, she would go with him to Beidaihe for summer vacation, and swimming there would be noble.

Saying that, she laughed again. However, tonight, he felt that Quli's laughter had a somewhat lewd smell.

A Hungry Crowd 206

— Ya Fei

Squeeze... squeeze... squeeze...

In front of the soup kitchen, a large crowd of people huddled together, dark and dense, the crowd tightly packed, heads bobbing incessantly; men, women, old, young, shouting, clamoring, crying, yelling, the surrounding air filled with dust and dirt. But the crowd continued to grow larger and larger.

Today, Uncle Chang came later, so he was squeezed to the outermost edge; he held a bowl, preparing to receive a bowl of porridge to take back, so that he, his old wife, and an eleven-year-old son, a family of three, could fill their long-starved bellies. But there were so many people, and maybe today, like the day before, he would have to go back with an empty bowl! Thinking this way, he felt heavy in his heart; so he used all his strength and desperately pushed forward. However, the front was still motionless, and many people surrounded him from behind. He was squeezed inside, suffocated and unable to breathe. He wanted to retreat and take a breath, but when he thought that the bowl he was holding under his arm was still empty, he finally had to endure the squeezing, and his two feet had already been lifted off the ground by about four or five inches. He floated and moved with the overturning of the crowd, and the two gates of the soup kitchen in front were still not open, but the door frames were squeezed particularly loudly; sometimes there was a burst of excitement in the front, and many people's heels were unable to stand firmly. Those strong men could still endure it, but the women and the elderly men and women really couldn't stand it. They could only shout for help inside!

Hundreds of people, each stretching their necks, staring with hundreds of pairs of eyes at the two doors of the soup kitchen, with hungry and anxious faces, constantly sighing in front of them!

"Damn it, aren't they opening the door today? Our arms are sore from standing." Uncle Chang really couldn't stand it anymore, he muttered angrily.

"Really, they were supposed to open the door by two o'clock in the afternoon. Today, there's no smoke coming out of the chimney, I'm afraid they won't open the door!" The young man standing next to Uncle Chang also said disappointedly. Uncle Chang also knew him, he was Jin Gen from the river pier on the opposite bank, and his family couldn't survive like his own. Originally, in these years, not to mention himself and Jin Gen, but everyone in the whole village was spinning in the hungry crowd. Years of war were mixed with great floods, and the rich had all fled to the cities. Now there were so many bandits in the countryside, and everywhere was robbing and clamoring for hunger. In such days, the villagers were really suffering. Which family in the whole village could eat a full meal of rice, anyway, no one could even get hold of chaff! And God insisted on taking the lives of the poor: so this year there was such an unprecedented drought, and the harvest was empty, but the land rent and grain tax were not afraid that you would be short of a penny. In the days to come, I really don't know how to get through it; today, tomorrow, the day after tomorrow, and the day after tomorrow... The more he thought about it, the more painful he felt, and a hundred knots had been tied in his stomach. He simply didn't dare to think about it anymore.

"The factory has not received rice, the porridge is temporarily suspended, this announcement." Suddenly, someone came to hang a white sign on the door of the soup kitchen. Then there was a burst of noise, and hundreds of heads flickered again in the sunlight, disappointed faces, hungry eyes, crying, shouting, and sighing sounds, mixed together, almost shaking the world.

The New Policy of Kidnappers: Small Profits and Quick Turnover 207

— Pi

The other day, a student of a certain elementary school was kidnapped. Fortunately, it was noticed immediately, and the hostage was recovered. The police arrested a kidnapper. According to his confession, it is now difficult to do big kidnappings, because to do big kidnappings, you must use pistols and rent cars, which makes it easy to find clues. In case of failure, it often leads to bloodshed and even a loss. Therefore, he has now changed his policy and specializes in doing small kidnappings. He does not need pistols, nor does he need cars. The capital is relatively light, and the kidnapping is easy. The price of each hostage is only 500 yuan, which is easy for the kidnapped to pay. This is really a kidnapper who believes in small profits and quick turnover. Now the business is not good, so he uses the principle of small profits and quick turnover to attract customers at low prices. Unexpectedly, the kidnappers also use this method to specialize in small hostages. This is really a unique aspect of kidnapping.

Occasional Words from the Study 208

— Philosopher

(3) Heroism

A child has no sense of self-worth. He does not know the position of mankind in the universe or the position of the individual in society. He only opens his curious eyes to observe the things around him, but ignores the thing called "self," so he has no pain. But when a child grows up and can use reason to think, the question, "What kind of reality am I, what kind of existence am I?" will probably bother him all day long. So he begins to draw a yardstick from the experiences, knowledge, and understanding of things accumulated in his memory, and measures the position of mankind in the vast universe and the position of the individual in the complex social structure. Self-evaluation is slowly formed. However, the evaluation at this time often exceeds the actual value of the "self," and because of this exaggerated evaluation, young people often have strong self-confidence, vigorous spirit, and are full of fantasies hung in mid-air, and regard life as an open road full of roses. When he walks out of the school gate, leaves the wings of his parents, and enters society alone, in the process of the struggle between the subjective "self" and the objective "non-self," he will find the weakness of the "self" and the errors in the numerical evaluation of himself, right? The "self" originally has no free will, no power, and is completely determined by the things of the "non-self"! Eternal tragedy begins from here. The center of all thoughts, experiences, knowledge, reason, and spiritual reserves collapses in an instant. In such a time, can people still survive?

But if you can't survive, what can you do? So individual human nature diverges, and society also has a myriad of different aspects. Some become skeptics,

Page 20

Page 21

some become nihilists, some become Fausts and Don Quixotes, some go to insane asylums, some go to sleep on train tracks, and all kinds of thoughts and philosophies of life arise from here.

The destiny of life is an eternal tragedy: this is an objective and ever-present proposition of truth. Whether you learn from Shakyamuni to cut off the six thieves, break the five emotions, and eliminate the senses so that you cannot experience the suffering of life, or learn from Baudelaire to smoke opium and indulge in lust to numb yourself, the tragic fate will always cruelly arrive. Avoiding pain is a seemingly clever, but actually foolish method, and isn't such a despicable and cowardly attitude precisely the attitude that we should despise?

Regarding life, we should not close our eyes, but bravely face it, admit that it is an inevitable tragedy, and resist it, using the spirit of struggle as the foundation of our lives. Isn't that kind of heroism what we should admire? Let us learn from the camel, learn from the lion, learn from the baby! Like the camel, endure hardships and work hard to understand life, like the lion, destroy the traditional life, destroy all compromises and avoidances, and then be a baby again to reaffirm and recreate! The civilization and happiness of mankind are not obtained by following the destiny of history like the materialists, but are the result of fighting heroism. Let us, this group of sufferers, demand our own fighting power and our own will.

Adrift 209

East, West, South, North 210

— San Duo

Paris Dispatch, Death Ray Gun Successfully Tested. According to engineer Clerc-Masse of the Ministry of Labor, he and his brother and an Austrian engineer named Rielhaus have succeeded after two years of testing. The function of the gun is not to kill people, but to make people temporarily lose consciousness, like being drunk.

It seems too wasteful to spend the efforts of three people and two years to invent something that only makes people "drunk". On the eve of World War II, we should invent killing weapons with effects above "drunkenness"; but France is not doing this. A friend who studied in France said that French women are the most lovely. I said that the engineer is even more lovely.

We Chinese are not willing to waste time and money like this. You invent as much as you like. You must know that the antiques in the old country are no less than the new gadgets. Just like this year's drought, the Soviet Union spent time and money to invent artificial rain, but our 63rd generation Zhang Tianshi only needs to set up an altar to perform rituals, and wouldn't it rain heavily?

However, I heard that Zhang Tianshi has committed suicide five times for some reason. I hope that he will quickly pass on all his magical powers to the 64th generation before he dies, otherwise, even toys that only cause "drunkenness" will be impossible to resist.

Fiction

Liu Desheng in Jiangxi (2) 211

— Wan Guoan

"Fellow, wake up, don't sleep!"

Hei Da Ge was dreaming of playing Pai Gow with his brothers and got a pair of "Plum Blossom Nine" and wanted to "eat it all," but he was awakened by someone. How disappointing! He turned over and sat up, cursing unclearly:

"Damn your uncle! I still..." He just cursed to this point, opened his eyes and took a look, and something was wrong! Three soldiers wearing tattered gray military uniforms who looked neither like soldiers nor like ordinary people were standing in front of him with guns in their hands.

"What are you doing?"

"We are the Red Army!"

These two words, Red Army, seemed to hit Hei Da Ge hard with a strong neck crutch. It gave him a shiver!

"Let's go, fellow! There are benefits to going with us. Drinking, playing with women, you can have whatever you want?"

When Hei Liu Ge heard that there were women to play with, he became confused. Anyway, he was useless. If he hadn't fallen asleep, wouldn't you three skinny ghosts be my prisoners? It's okay to go with you, let me, a Shandong guy, taste what a fellow province woman tastes like. He was thinking to himself while slowly climbing up. Hei Da Ge stood up, his two skinny legs were still a little weak, and he patted the dust on his butt with his hands. He had just taken two steps forward when he felt even more uncomfortable! He understood in his heart that his crutch was gone!

"Give me the gun,"

He said while reaching out to take it, but suddenly he got a kick in the butt, and the skinny guy cursed fiercely:

"You don't want to live, fellow! Don't you know that your gun has been confiscated?"

"I'm using it as a crutch."

"I think you look like a crutch, you bastard!"

National Studies 213

Miss Bingmei's Selected Tang Poems

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM

Song of Everlasting Regret (Continued)

The wind blows her fairy sleeves, fluttering and rising,

As if dancing the Rainbow Skirt and Feathered Coat Dance.

Her jade face is lonely, tears streaming down,

Like a pear blossom, with spring bringing rain.

Full of emotion and tears, she bids farewell to the Emperor,

One parting, voice and face are lost in the vastness.

In Zhaoyang Palace, love and affection are severed,

In Penglai Palace, days and months stretch long.

Turning her head to look down at the mortal world,

She cannot see Chang'an, only dust and mist.

Only by sending old objects to express her deep affection,

She sends a gilded box and a hairpin.

One strand of the hairpin remains, joined to one fan,

The hairpin is split, the gold is divided, the gilded box separated.

But let the heart be as firm as the gilded box,

And they will meet in heaven or on earth.

Before parting, she earnestly sends words again,

In the words, there is a vow known to both hearts.

On the seventh day of the seventh month, in the Hall of Longevity,

At midnight, when no one is around, they whisper secretly.

In heaven, they wish to be birds that fly wing to wing,

On earth, they wish to be trees with intertwined branches.

Heaven and earth may have an end,

But this regret will never cease.

Storytelling to Music 215

Yao Xiaoan Pang Xueqing Pearl Pagoda

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening: Sweeping Qin

Don't laugh at my crazy, foolish, and filthy appearance. The Bodhisattva of the Underworld intentionally descends to the mortal world. He borrows a body to sit in meditation at Lingyin Temple. He writes poems on the wall to sweep away the Qin. The current prime minister comes to burn incense. Three sticks of pure incense held in his hands. He lowers his head and silently communicates with the spirits. He only hopes for favorable weather and good harvests. He only seeks for the husband and wife to have longevity. He blesses the virtuous father and sons of the Yue family. May they ascend to the immortal realm and be reborn soon. He raises his head and suddenly sees the poem left behind. The treacherous hero trembles with fear. This poem was made with the lady. When the matter is exposed, a raging fire arises. Immediately, he angrily calls for the mad monk. He knows that his words are full of Zen secrets and transformations. He can summon wind and rain and is capable of everything. He holds a fire tube to communicate with foreign countries. He also holds a palm broom to sweep away treacherous officials. The storm arises because of the exclusive power. He dies with resentment at Lengquan Pavilion. Returning home, the husband and wife discuss together. They shave their heads and convert to Buddhism, renouncing fame and wealth. They listen to the slanderous words of long-tongued women. They endure all the tortures of the Fengdu hell. Now, his whole body is cast in iron at Yue Wang's tomb.
